المرصد الرابع - المقصد الخامس : في أقسام الواحد الواحد بالنسبة ثم الواحد الشخصي إن لم يقبل انقساماً أصلاً لا بحسب الأجزاء المقدارية، ولا بحسب غيرها محمولة كانت أو غير محمولة، وهو المسمى بالواحد الحقيقي أولى مما يقبل الانقسام بوجه ما والوحدة التي من أقسام الواحد الحقيقي أولى من غيرها. والواحد بالاتصال أولى من الواحد بالاجتماع، وإذا كانت مقولية الوحدة على وحدات تلك الأقسام بالتشكيك ( فتكون تلك الوحدات مختلفة بالحقيقة)، متشاركة في هذا العارض الذي هو مفهوم الوحدة مطلقاً، على قياس اختلاف الوجودات الخاصة بالحقائق، مع الاشتراك في العارض الذي هو الوجود المطلق . ( فلا يجب ) حينئذ ( اشتراكها ) أي اشتراك الوحدات ( في الحكم)، فيجوز أن يبنى على ذلك ويقال : ( فمنها ما هو وجودي كالوحدة الاتصالية والاجتماعية على ما سيأتي، ( ومنها ما هو اعتباري محض فلا يلزم من وجودية الوحدة تسلسل في الأمور الموجودة؛ لجواز الانتهاء إلى وحدة اعتبارية، ولا يلزم من عدميتها في الجملة كونها اعتبارية على الإطلاق ، ( ومنها ما هو زائد ) على ماهية الواحد، كوحدة الإنسان مثلاً، ( ومنها ما هو نفس الماهية كوحدة الوحدة فإنها واحدة بذاتها، لا بوحدة زائدة عليها، ( ومنها ما هو جزؤها ) أي يجوز كونها جزءاً منها، وكذلك سائر الأحكام) فيقال مثلاً جاز كونها جوهراً في بعض، وعرضاً في بعض آخر، فتنبه له أي لما ذكرناه من جواز اختلاف الوحدات في الأحكام، فإنه ينفعك في مواضع متعددة.
قوله : ( والوحدة التي من أقسام إلخ لأنه لا يمكن تصور انفكاك الوحدة عنها، فالتصور والمتصور فيها كلاهما محالان بخلاف القسمين الباقيين أعني النقطة والمفارق، فإنه يمكن تصور انفكاك الوحدة عنهما، وإن كان التصور محالاً. وما قاله الشارح قدس سره في حواشي شرح التجريد من كون الواجب تعالى الذي هو فرد من المفارق لعدم قبوله القسمة إلى الأجزاء أصلاً أولى بالوحدة من الوحدة الشخصية فمبني على كون التشخص جزءاً منها، كما صرح به فيها، فلا تدافع بين الكلامين ولا احتياج إلى تكلف بارد بأن يحمل الواحد الحقيقي في قوله : وهو المسمى بالواحد الحقيقي على معنى ما لا يقبل الانقسام إلى الأجزاء أصلاً، وفي قوله : من أقسام الواحد الحقيقي على معنى ما لا يقبل الانقسام إلى الأجزاء المقدارية، وأن يصرف قوله : أصلاً فيما تقدم عن معناه الظاهر إلى معنى لا حقيقة ولا حساً.
قوله : ( وإذا كانت مقولية إلخ) لا يخفى أن اللازم مما ذكر كون الواحد مقولاً على ما تحته بالتشكيك والمقصود كون الوحدة بالنسبة إلى أفرادها كذلك قدر الشارح قدس سره الشرطية وجعل ضمير فيكون راجعاً إلى الوحدات لكن الكلام في لزوم كون الوحدة كذلك مما تقدم. ووجه اللزوم أنه لما كان الواحد باعتبار معنى الوحدة مقولاً بالتشكيك على أفراده، كان حصول الوحدة في معروضاتها مختلفة، فكان بعض أفراد الوحدة أولى بالوحدة من البعض الآخر أيضاً، فتدبر. وأنت خبير بأن الاقتضاء أمر ثبوتي فالاتصاف به يقتضي أحد الوجودين وبه يتم الكلام فتأمل. قوله : ( والوحدة من أقسام الواحد الحقيقي إلخ) الظاهر أن المراد بالواحد الحقيقي الذي جعل الوحدة من أقسامها هو الذي مر في صدر المقصد، أعني ما لا ينقسم إلى الأجزاء المقدارية أصلاً، لا الواحد الحقيقي المذكور بقوله : وهو المسمى بالواحد الحقيقي؛ لأن كون الوحدة من أقسام الواحد الحقيقي بهذا المعنى إنما يتم إذا لم يتركب من الأجزاء الذهنية أيضاً، وبهذا التوجيه يندفع ما يتوهم من أن ما ذكره هاهنا مخالف لما ذكره في حواشي التجريد، حيث قال ثمة : ثم الواحد بالشخص إذا لم يقبل انقساماً أصلاً، لا بحسب الأجزاء الكمية أي المقدارية، ولا بحسب الأجزاء الحدية أي غير المقدارية سواء كانت محمولة أو غير محمولة، فإنها توجد جميع في الحد أيضاً، كما مر ولا بحسب الماهية والشخص كالواجب تعالى كان أولى بالوحدة من ما عداه ثم المنقسم بحسب الماهية والتشخص فقط كالوحدة الشخصية أولى مما ينقسم باعتبار آخر كالنقطة والمفارق . ووجه الاندفاع أن المراد بالواحد الشخصي في قوله : ثم الواحد الشخصي إن لم يقبل انقساماً إلخ هو الواجب تعالى والمراد بقوله: والوحدة التي من أقسام الواحد الحقيقي أولى من غيرها أنها أولى أقسام الواحد الحقيقي بالمعنى العام سوى الواجب تعالى بقرينة أنه صرح أولاً بأنه أولى من الكل فيؤول إلى ما ذكره في شرح التجريد، فتأمل .
قوله : ( فتكون تلك الوحدات إلخ) أي يجوز أن يكون كذلك.
قوله : ( ولا يلزم من عدميتها في الجملة أي باعتبار بعض أفرادها كونها اعتبارية باعتبار جميع الأفراد، بخلاف ما إذا كانت متحدة الماهية فإنه لا يجوز اختلاف أفرادها بالوجود والعدم، لما مر مراراً من أن كل ما من شأنه الوجود في الخارج لا يجوز الاتصاف به إلا بعد وجوده، فيه؛ كيلا يلزم السفسطة .
أقسام الواحد الحقيقي أولى من غيرها أنها أولى أقسام الواحد الحقيقي بالمعنى العام سوى الواجب تعالى بقرينة أنه صرح أولاً بأنه أولى من الكل فيؤول إلى ما ذكره في شرح التجريد،
فتأمل .
قوله : ( فتكون تلك الوحدات مختلفة بالحقيقة) أي يجوز أن يكون كذلك، على ما مر من الشارح في بحث الوجود، وإنما فرع على التشكيك لأنه يظهر حينئذ . قوله : (جاز كونها جوهراً في بعض) أي ليس عرضية الوحدة في بعض مانع لجوهريتها في بعض آخر، لا أن جوهريتها في بعض جائز.
The Fourth Observation - Fifth Section: On the divisions of the one. The one in relation, then the individual one if it does not accept division at all, neither according to quantitative parts nor according to other than them, whether predicable or not predicable, and it is called the true one, is prior to what accepts division in some respect, and the unity that is among the divisions of the true one is prior to other than it. And the one by connection is prior to the one by conjunction. And if the predictation of unity upon the unities of those divisions is by tashkik (gradation), then those unities are different in reality, sharing in this accident which is the concept of unity absolutely, analogous to the difference of specific existences in realities while sharing in the accident which is absolute existence. Then it is not necessary that they share in the judgment, so it is permissible to build upon that and say: among them is what is existential, like the unity of connection and conjunction as will come, and among them is what is purely relational; so no regress in existing things follows from the existentiality of unity, because it is possible to end at a relational unity, and nor does its non-existentiality in general entail its being relational absolutely; and among them is what is additional to the quiddity of the one, like the unity of man for example; and among them is what is the quiddity itself, like the unity of unity, for it is one by itself, not by an additional unity; and among them is what is its part, i.e., it is permissible for it to be a part of it; and likewise the rest of the judgments, so one says for example: it is permissible for it to be a substance in some and an accident in some other. So be attentive, i.e., to what we have mentioned of the permissibility of the difference of unities in judgments, for it benefits you in many places. His saying: 'And the unity that is among the divisions, etc.' because it is impossible to conceive the disengagement of unity from it, so both the conception and the conceived are impossible, unlike the remaining two types, namely the point and the separate (al-mufariq), for it is possible to conceive the disengagement of unity from them, even if the conception is impossible. And what the commentator (quddisa sirruh) said in the glosses on Sharh al-Tajrid concerning the Necessary being—who is an individual of the separate—being prior to individual unity is based on individuation being a part of it, as he stated there, so there is no contradiction between the two statements and no need for a forced interpretation that interprets 'the true one' in his saying 'it is called the true one' as meaning what does not accept division into parts at all, and in his saying 'among the divisions of the true one' as meaning what does not accept division into quantitative parts, and to divert his saying 'at all' from its apparent meaning to a meaning of neither in reality nor in sense. His saying: 'And if the predictation, etc.' It is not hidden that what follows from what was mentioned is that the one is said of what is under it by tashkik, and the intended meaning is that unity with respect to its individuals is likewise. The commentator (quddisa sirruh) predicated the conditional and made the pronoun refer to the unities, but the discussion is about the necessity of unity being thus from what preceded. And the aspect of necessity is that when the one, by virtue of the meaning of unity, is said by tashkik of its individuals, then the occurrence of unity in its substrates is different, so some individuals of unity are prior to unity over others, so reflect. And you are an expert that requirement is a positive matter, so being described by it requires one of the two existences, and by it the speech is completed, so contemplate. His saying: 'And the unity from the divisions of the true one, etc.' The apparent meaning is that what is meant by 'the true one' of which unity is made a division is that which passed at the beginning of the section, i.e., what is not divided into quantitative parts at all, not the true one mentioned in his saying 'it is called the true one'; because unity being among the divisions of the true one in this sense is only completed if it is not composed of intellectual parts also. And by this direction, what is imagined of contradiction between what he mentioned here and what he mentioned in the glosses on al-Tajrid is repelled, where he said there: Then the individual one, if it does not accept division at all, neither according to quantitative parts nor according to limit-parts (i.e., other than quantitative) whether predicable or not predicable—for they all exist in the limit also as has passed—nor according to quiddity and individuation, like the Necessary (exalted), is prior in unity to what is other than it; then what is divided according to quiddity and individuation only, like individual unity, is prior to what is divided in another respect, like the point and the separate. And the aspect of repulsion is that what is meant by 'the individual one' in his saying 'then the individual one if it does not accept division, etc.' is the Necessary (exalted), and what is meant by his saying 'and the unity that is among the divisions of the true one is prior to other than it' is that it is the prior of the divisions of the true one in the general sense except the Necessary, by the indication that he stated first that it is prior to all, so it reverts to what he mentioned in Sharh al-Tajrid, so reflect. His saying: 'Then those unities, etc.' i.e., it is permissible for it to be so. His saying: 'And it does not follow from their non-existentiality in general' i.e., by considering some of their individuals being relational by considering all individuals, unlike if they were of one quiddity, for then it is not permissible for their individuals to differ in existence and non-existence, as has been repeated that everything that is apt to exist in the external world is not permissible to be described by it except after its existence in it, so that sophistry does not follow. The divisions of the true one are prior to other than them: they are the prior divisions of the true one in the general sense except the Necessary, by the indication that he stated first that it is prior to all, so it reverts to what he mentioned in Sharh al-Tajrid, so reflect. His saying: 'Then those unities are different in reality' i.e., it is permissible for it to be so, according to what the commentator said in the discussion of existence, and he only made it conditional on tashkik because it becomes apparent then. His saying: 'It is permissible for it to be a substance in some' i.e., the accidentalness of unity in some does not prevent its substantiality in some other, not that its substantiality in some is permissible.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification passage that also addresses an objection. It begins by defining the true one (al-wahid al-haqiqi) as that which admits no division whatsoever—not quantitative, not predicamental, not quidditative. It then establishes that this true one is prior to anything that admits division in some respect. The commentator then explains that the unity which is a division of the true one (i.e., the unity of that true one) is itself prior to other unities. He then lists the types of unity: existential unity (like unity of connection or assembly), purely relational unity, unity additional to the quiddity, unity identical with the quiddity, and unity that is a part of the quiddity. He notes that these unities differ in judgments (e.g., some are substances, some accidents) and that this differentiation is possible because the predication of unity upon its instances is by tashkik (gradation), not univocity. A significant portion of the passage is devoted to resolving an apparent contradiction between this text and the commentator's own remarks in the glosses on Sharh al-Tajrid. The commentator explains that 'the true one' mentioned first refers to the Necessary Being, while 'the true one' in a later line refers to a narrower sense (not divisible into quantitative parts only), thereby reconciling the statements. He also clarifies that the priority of the Necessary Being's unity over individual unity does not conflict with the priority of individual unity over other unities, because the Necessary is excluded from the comparison. The passage thus tightens the definition of true unity and its types while defending textual consistency.

Key Terms
الواحد الحقيقي
الواجب تعالى
شرح التجريد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The same term 'true one' is used inconsistently, showing a contradiction in al-Jurjani's thought.
Correction: Al-Jurjani himself shows the term is used in two distinct senses, and once distinguished, there is no contradiction.

Checkpoint
What does al-Jurjani say resolves the apparent contradiction between the text and the gloss?
A) The gloss was written earlier and is superseded.
B) 'True one' has two different meanings in the two passages.
C) The priority is only metaphorical.
D) The gloss refers to a different kind of unity.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in the tradition can often be resolved by recognizing that key terms are used in different, well-defined senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever avoided studying theology because you assumed contradictions among scholars were irreconcilable? After this lesson, what specific step can you take the next time you encounter a doctrinal contradiction instead of dismissing it?
?
When you read the statement 'the unity of the true one is prior' in this passage, did you instinctively attach a single meaning to 'true one'? What does this reveal about how your own assumptions can lead to misunderstandings of Allah's attributes, and how will you guard against that in your study of tawhid?

What Is Kalam?

The Definition of 'Two are Different' and the Condition of Existence
States the definition of 'two are different' and explains the condition of existence for taghayur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of 'two are different' in kalam, the majority view that twoness entails difference, and the teachers' refinement that taghayur requires existence.

Core Idea
Difference (taghayur) is a positive attribute that only applies to existents.

This passage tackles a foundational logical issue: what does it mean for two things to be 'different'? While the majority held that any two are automatically different, the teachers (mashayikh) introduced a key condition – existence. Understanding this condition illuminates the nature of positive attributes and their scope.

Guided Path
1
Review the types of relations
The passage begins by listing various relations (similarity, equality, etc.) as background. Notice how these are specific kinds of relations between two things.
These examples set the stage for the central definition.
2
Focus on the core definition
Read the claim 'the two are the different' (الاثنان هما الغيران). Understand the majority interpretation: twoness entails difference. Then contrast with the teachers' view that not every two are different.
Pay attention to the phrase 'مشهور الذي ذهب إليه الجمهور'.
3
Understand the condition of existence
Why do teachers exclude non-existents? Because otherness (ghayriyya) is a positive attribute (sifah thubutiyyah). You will see that existence is necessary for difference.
The passage concludes that the existent is distinct from the non-existent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران . الكيف مشابهة، وفي الكم مساواة، وفي الشكل مشاكلة، وفي الوضع موازاة ومحاذاة ؛ كشخصين تساويا في الوضع بالقياس إلى ثالث، وفي الأطراف مطابقة ؛ كطاسين أطبق طرف أحدهما على طرف الآخر، وفي النسبة مناسبة ؛ كزيد وعمرو إذا تشاركا في بنوة بكر. المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران . الاثنان هما الغيران أي الاثنينية تستلزم التغاير هذا هو المشهور الذي ذهب إليه الجمهور، فكل اثنين عندهم غيران كما أن كل غيرين اثنين اتفاقاً . وقال مشايخنا : ليس كل اثنين بغيرين بل الغيران موجودان جاز انفكاكهما في حيز أو عدم فخرج بقيد الوجود الأعدام فإنها لا توصف بالتغاير عندهم؛ بناء على أن الغيرية الصفات الثبوتية فلا يتصف به عدمان، ولا عدم ووجود وهذا أعم من قوله : إذ لا تمايز فيها، ولا بد في الغيرين من التمايز وذلك لاختصاصه بما يكون طرفاه عدميين . وذلك لأن الموجود ممتاز عن المعدوم
The Fourth Lookout - Seventh Objective: The two are the different. In quality: similarity; in quantity: equality; in shape: correspondence; in position: parallelism and adjacency, like two persons equal in position relative to a third; in extremities: matching, like two bowls whose rim of one matches the rim of the other; in relation: proportionality, like Zayd and 'Amr if both share descent from Bakr. Seventh Objective: The two are the different. 'The two are the different' means that twoness entails difference (taghayur). This is the well-known view of the majority; so every two according to them are different, just as every two different are two by agreement. And our teachers said: Not every two are different; rather, the different (al-ghayran) are two existents whose separation in locus or non-[separation] is possible. So by the condition of existence, they exclude non-existents (al-a'dam), for they are not described as difference (taghayur) according to them, based on the fact that otherness (al-ghayriyya) is a positive attribute (sifah thubutiyyah); so neither two non-existents nor a non-existent and an existent can be described by it. And this is more general than his statement: 'since there is no distinction (tamyiz) in them, and distinction is necessary in the two different, and that is because it is specific to what has both extreme terms non-existent.' And that is because the existent is distinct from the non-existent.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage defines the relationship between 'two' and 'different' in a kalam/logical context. It begins by listing various types of relations (similarity, equality, etc.) as background, but the core is the Seventh Objective: 'The two are the different.' The commentary explains that this means twoness entails difference (taghayur), which is the position of the majority: every pair is a pair of different things. However, the author's teachers (Mashayikhuna) hold that not every two are different; the term 'different' (al-ghayran) specifically refers to two existents that can be separated in locus. They exclude non-existents (al-a'dam) because otherness (ghayriyya) is a positive attribute (sifah thubutiyyah), and non-existents lack existence, so they cannot possess such an attribute. This exclusion also covers a non-existent and an existent. The commentary then notes that this definition is more general than the author's original statement that 'there is no distinction (tamyiz) in non-existents, and distinction is necessary for the two different,' because that statement is specific to cases where both extremes are non-existent. The passage concludes by affirming that the existent is distinct from the non-existent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think any two things, including non-existents, are automatically different.
Correction: This passage clarifies that taghayur is a positive attribute requiring existence, so non-existents cannot be described as different.

Checkpoint
According to the teachers (Mashayikhuna), why are non-existents not considered 'different' (ghayran)?
A) Because non-existents are identical to each other
B) Because otherness (ghayriyya) is a positive attribute, and non-existents lack existence
C) Because non-existents cannot be separated in locus
D) Because non-existents are not two

Key Takeaway
The term 'different' (al-ghayran) is reserved for two existents that can be separated in locus, because otherness is a positive attribute requiring existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If otherness (taghayur) is a positive attribute that only applies to existents, how does that reshape your understanding of your own identity? Are you tempted to define yourself by differences that are merely mental constructs rather than real attributes grounded in existence? How will you ensure your sense of self is rooted in what truly exists—your relationship with Allah—rather than in illusions of separation?
?
The teachers taught that two non-existents cannot be considered different. When you hold grudges or dwell on disputes, do you realize that the 'difference' you feel might be based on something that does not truly exist? If difference requires existence, what does that mean for the reality of animosity in your heart? Will you let go of imagined divisions and focus on the shared existence that connects you to others as Allah's creation?
?
The passage says 'the existent is distinct from the non-existent.' How often do you confuse what is real and lasting with what is temporal and void? Does your anxiety or pride come from exaggerating the 'existence' of temporary circumstances? Commit to recognizing that only Allah and His commands have true existence and permanence—how will you reorient your priorities today to reflect that reality?

What Is Kalam?

Defining Two Different Things: The Condition of Separation
Definition of 'two different things' with conditions of separation and locus/non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of 'two different things' (al-ghayran) in Islamic theology, including the key condition of possibility of separation and why inseparable entities are not considered different.

Core Idea
Two things are different only if they can be separated from each other.

The concept of 'two different things' (al-ghayran) is fundamental in kalam discussions about attributes, parts, and existence. This passage from al-Mawaqif defines this term by specifying what it excludes and what conditions must hold. You will see why inseparable entities like an attribute and its subject are not considered 'two different things' and how the definition covers both spatial and non-spatial entities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the flow: the definition starts by excluding certain cases, then states the condition of separation, then gives examples, and finally expands the scope.
Pay attention to the key term 'جواز الانفكاك' (possibility of separation).
2
Identify the core condition
The central condition for two things to be considered different is that separation between them must be possible (يجوز الانفكاك). Understand that this is a real, existential separation, not merely conceptual.
This condition excludes inseparable pairs like attribute and described.
3
Examine the examples provided
The passage gives two examples: attribute with its described subject, and part with its whole. These are not two different things because they cannot be separated from each other. Notice the reasoning: the attribute is neither identical to the described nor other than it in the relevant sense.
The Arabic says: 'لا هو ولا غيره' (neither it nor other).
4
Understand the scope phrase
The definition adds 'in a locus or non-existence' to cover both spatial entities (bodies, atoms) and non-spatial entities (attributes). This ensures the definition applies to all possible pairs.
Spatial entities are those that occupy space, like bodies; attributes are non-spatial.
5
Reflect on the exclusions
The passage also explicitly excludes states (aḥwāl) and the pair of an existent and a non-existent. States are excluded because they are not real entities. The existent/non-existent pair is excluded because they cannot be considered two things of the same type.
The exclusion of existent/non-existent is based on the commentator's reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خرج به الأحوال أيضاً؛ إذ لا نثبتها، فلا يتصور اتصافها بالغيرية. وكذا يلزم أن يخرج به اثنان أحدهما موجود والآخر معدوم. ( و ) خرج بقيد جواز الانفكاك ( ما لا ينفك ) أي ما لا يجوز انفكاكهما، ( كالصفة مع الموصوف، والجزء مع الكل، فإنه ) أي المذكور الذي هو الصفة والجزء ( لا هو ولا غيره ) أي ليس الصفة عين الموصوف ولا الجزء عين الكل، وهو ظاهر وليسا أيضاً غير الموصوف، وغير الكل؛ إذ لا يجوز الانفكاك بينهما من الجانبين، وهو معتبر عندهم في الغيرين. (و) قولهم ( في حيز أو عدم ليشمل المتحيز (وغيره) وكان الشيخ الأشعري قد عرف معنى. قوله : ( إذ لا نثبتها ) أي إخراجهم الأحوال بناء على عدم القول بها، لا بناء على أنها ليست من أفراد الغيرين كالعدمين. وأما ما قيل من أن إخراج ما ليس عندهم مما لا له، فمدفوع بأن المراد خرج ما يقول به البعض. قوله : ( وكذا يلزم إلخ ما مر من قوله : ولا عدم ووجود كان بياناً لعدم كونهما من أفراد المحدود؛ بناء على دليل الشارح قدس سره، دون دليل المصنف وهذا بيان لخروجهما عن الحد، فلا تكرار وإنما قال يلزم أن يخرج، ولم يقل : يخرج إشارة إلى عدم تصريحهم بخروجهما، لكنه يلزم من حدهم وإلى استبعاده، فإن القول بأن الواجب تعالى ليس عين المعدومات ولا غيرها مما يأباه العقل السليم. قوله ليشمل المتحيز وغيره) أي التعميم لأجل الشمول المذكور، وأما التقييد بهما : فلإخراج جواز الانفكاك فيما عداهما من الصفات، فلا يرد أن ترك التقييد بهما كاف في الشمول. والمراد بالمتحيز المتحير بالذات وهو الجسم والجوهر الفرد، قديماً كان أو حادثاً، وغير المتحيز بالذات الصفات القائمة بالموصوفات المتعددة، فإنه لم يجز الانفكاك بينهما في التحيز، لكن يجوز في العدم، وليس المراد به المفارق لأنهم لا يقولون به.
It excludes the states (aḥwāl) as well, since we do not affirm them, so their being described with otherness (al-ghayriyya) is inconceivable. And likewise it necessarily excludes two things one of which is existent and the other non-existent. And by the condition of possibility of separation (jawāz al-infikāk), it excludes what does not separate—i.e., what is not permissible to separate from each other, like the attribute with the described, and the part with the whole. For it, i.e., the mentioned which is the attribute and the part, is neither it nor other—i.e., the attribute is not identical to the described, nor the part identical to the whole—and that is apparent, and they are also not other than the described and other than the whole, because separation between them is not permissible from both sides, and that is considered among them for the two different things. And their saying 'in a locus (ḥayyiz) or non-existence' to include the spatial (al-mutaḥayyiz) and other than it. And al-Shaykh al-Ashʿarī had defined the meaning. His saying: 'since we do not affirm them'—i.e., their exclusion of the states is based on not affirming them, not based on their not being instances of the two different things like non-existents. As for what was said—that excluding what is not according to them is of no benefit—it is refuted by saying that the intended meaning is that it excludes what some people affirm. His saying: 'And likewise it necessarily excludes, etc.'—what passed from his saying: 'nor non-existence and existence' was an explanation of their not being instances of the defined term, based on the proof of the commentator (may his secret be sanctified), not the proof of the author, and this is an explanation of their exclusion from the definition, so there is no repetition. He only said 'it necessarily excludes' and did not say 'it excludes' to indicate that they did not explicitly state their exclusion, but it follows from their definition, and to indicate its improbability, for the statement that the Necessary (al-Wājib)—may He be exalted—is neither identical to non-existents nor other than them is something that sound intellect abhors. His saying: 'to include the spatial and other than it'—i.e., the generalization for the mentioned inclusiveness. As for the restriction to both (i.e., locus and non-existence), it is to exclude the possibility of separation in other attributes—so it is not objected that leaving the restriction to them is sufficient for inclusiveness. And what is meant by 'the spatial' is what is spatial by essence, which is the body and the indivisible atom (jawhar fard), whether eternal or originated. And what is not spatial by essence are the attributes subsisting in multiple described entities, for separation between them in spatiality is not permissible, but it is permissible in non-existence. And what is meant by it is not the separate (al-mufāriq) because they do not affirm it.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'two different things' (al-ghayrān) by listing what it excludes and the conditions for two things to be considered different. It begins by stating that the definition excludes states (aḥwāl) because the author's school does not affirm them as real entities; therefore they cannot be described as 'other' to anything. It also necessarily excludes the pair of one existent and one non-existent. Then the key condition is introduced: possibility of separation (jawāz al-infikāk). Anything that cannot be separated from its counterpart is not considered a different thing. Examples are the attribute and the described, and the part and the whole: the attribute is not identical to the described, nor is it other than it, because they cannot be separated from each other—they always coexist. The definition further adds the phrase 'in a locus or non-existence' to cover both spatial entities (like bodies) and non-spatial ones (like attributes). The commentator then explains the phrase 'since we do not affirm them' regarding the states: the exclusion is because the school does not affirm states, not because states are not instances of the two different things. He clarifies that the phrase 'nor non-existence and existence' in the definition is about the pair of existent and non-existent; this exclusion is based on the commentator's argument, not the author's, and it shows that such a pair cannot be considered two different things. The commentator also explains that 'in a locus or non-existence' is meant to be exhaustive: the restriction to these two categories is necessary to exclude possible separation in other attributes. Finally, he defines 'spatial' as what is spatial by essence, like bodies and atoms, while non-spatial entities are attributes that subsist in multiple described entities; these cannot be separated in spatial location but can be separated in non-existence.

Key Terms
الغيران
جواز الانفكاك
الصفة
الموصوف
الجزء
الكل
المتحيز
الحال
المعدوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An attribute and its described subject are considered two different things because they are distinct concepts.
Correction: They are not considered two different things because they cannot be separated from each other; separation in existence is not possible.

Checkpoint
Why does the definition of 'two different things' exclude the pair of an attribute and its described subject?
A) Because they are identical.
B) Because they cannot be separated from each other.
C) Because the attribute is not real.
D) Because they are both non-existent.

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'two different things' hinges on the real possibility of separation between two entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe your thoughts and your self are 'other'—but can they ever separate? This lesson says true difference requires possible separation. What does that reveal about your attachment to your own ideas?
?
If God's attributes are not 'other' than His essence because separation is impossible, what does that demand from your worship of Him? Are you treating His mercy or anger as something that can be separated from His oneness?
?
Everything in creation is defined by the possibility of separation. You will die—your soul will separate from your body. Are you living as if this separation is truly possible? When did you last let that fact change a decision?

Exclusion of States from the Definition of al-Ghayrān
Commentator explains why states are excluded from the definition of al-ghayrān.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ashʿarīs exclude states (ahwāl) from the definition of 'two different things' (al-ghayrān) and how this reflects their metaphysical commitments.

Core Idea
States are excluded not because they are non-existent, but because they are not affirmed as realities.

The commentator begins by noting that the definition of al-ghayrān excludes states (ahwāl), since the Ashʿarīs do not affirm the reality of states. This might seem like a trivial technicality, but it reveals a fundamental principle: only things that are actually established as real entities can be described as 'other' or 'not other'. In this lesson, we examine that exclusion and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on states
Read the Arabic sentence that states states are excluded because they are not established. Then read the translation.
The phrase 'lā nuthbituhā' is key.
2
Identify the rationale
Notice that the commentator specifies that the exclusion is not because states are like non-existents, but because they are simply not affirmed. This distinguishes the Ashʿarī position.
This relates to the broader debate on the reality of states.
3
Consider the objection and reply
The commentator addresses a potential objection: that excluding what one does not hold is irrelevant. The reply clarifies that the definition is meant to exclude what others (e.g., Muʿtazilites) affirm.
This shows the dialectical nature of kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد المرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران خرج به الأحوال أيضاً؛ إذ لا نثبتها، فلا يتصور اتصافها بالغيرية. وكذا يلزم أن يخرج به اثنان أحدهما موجود والآخر معدوم . ( و ) خرج بقيد جواز الانفكاك ( ما لا ينفك ) أي ما لا يجوز انفكاكهما ، ( كالصفة مع الموصوف ، والجزء مع الكل، فإنه ) أي المذكور الذي هو الصفة والجزء ( لا هو ولا غيره ) أي ليس الصفة عين الموصوف ولا الجزء عين الكل، وهو ظاهر وليسا أيضاً غير الموصوف، وغير الكل؛ إذ لا يجوز الانفكاك بينهما من الجانبين، وهو معتبر عندهم في الغيرين. (و) قولهم ( في حيز أو عدم ليشمل المتحيز (وغيره وكان الشيخ الأشعري قد عرف معنى قوله : ( إذ لا نثبتها ) أي إخراجهم الأحوال بناء على عدم القول بها، لا بناء على أنها ليست من أفراد الغيرين كالعدمين. وأما ما قيل من أن إخراج ما ليس عندهم مما لا له، فمدفوع بأن المراد خرج ما يقول به البعض. قوله : ( وكذا يلزم إلخ ما مر من قوله : ولا عدم ووجود كان بياناً لعدم كونهما من أفراد المحدود؛ بناء على دليل الشارح قدس سره، دون دليل المصنف وهذا بيان لخروجهما عن الحد، فلا تكرار وإنما قال يلزم أن يخرج، ولم يقل : يخرج إشارة إلى عدم تصريحهم بخروجهما، لكنه يلزم من حدهم وإلى استبعاده، فإن القول بأن الواجب تعالى ليس عين المعدومات ولا غيرها مما يأباه العقل السليم.
The Fourth Observatory - the Seventh Purpose: The two are the different ones. By this [definition] states (al-ahwāl) are also excluded, since we do not establish them, so it is not conceivable that they are described by otherness (al-ghayriyya). Likewise, it necessarily follows that two things, one of which is existent and the other non-existent, are excluded by it. And by the condition of the possibility of separation (jawāz al-infikāk) is excluded what does not separate, i.e., what does not permit their separation, like the attribute (al-ṣifa) with the qualified (al-mawṣūf), and the part (al-juzʾ) with the whole (al-kull). For the mentioned thing, which is the attribute and the part, is neither the same nor other: i.e., the attribute is not identical to the qualified, nor the part identical to the whole, which is obvious, and they are also not other than the qualified and other than the whole, since separation between them from both sides is not permissible, and that [i.e., permissibility of separation from both sides] is considered [valid] for the two different things (al-ghayrān). And their statement 'in existence or non-existence' is to include the spatially extended (al-mutaḥayyiz) and other than it. And Shaykh al-Ashʿarī had defined. His statement: 'since we do not establish them' means their exclusion of states is based on not affirming them, not on the grounds that they are not individuals of the two different things like the two non-existents. As for what was said, that excluding what they do not have is [a case of] what is not for him, it is repelled by [saying] that what is intended is that what some affirm is excluded. His statement: 'and likewise it necessarily follows, etc.' [refers to] what previously passed from his statement 'and not non-existence and existence' as an explanation that they are not individuals of the defined, based on the proof of the commentator (quddisa sirruhu), not on the proof of the author. And this is an explanation of their exclusion from the definition, so there is no repetition. He only said 'it necessarily follows that it is excluded' and did not say 'it is excluded' as an indication that their exclusion is not explicitly stated by them, but it follows necessarily from their definition, and as an indication of its improbability, for the statement that the Necessary (al-wājib taʿālā) is not identical to the non-existents nor other than them is something that sound reason rejects.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of 'al-ghayrān' (two different things). It begins by noting that the definition excludes states (al-ahwāl), because the Ashʿarīs do not affirm states as real entities—they are not established, so they cannot be described as 'other' or 'not other'. Next, it explains that the definition also excludes a pair where one is existent and the other non-existent, since non-existents are not considered individuals of the defined. The main point is that the definition includes a condition: the possibility of separation (jawāz al-infikāk) from both sides. This excludes pairs that cannot be separated, such as an attribute and its qualified subject (e.g., knowledge cannot be separated from the knower), and a part and its whole (e.g., a hand cannot be separated from the body in the sense of being a different entity). Such pairs are neither identical (they are not the same) nor other (they cannot exist apart). The commentator then explains the phrase 'in existence or non-existence' as an addition by some to include spatially extended things and non-spatially extended things under the definition. After quoting Shaykh al-Ashʿarī's definition, the commentator glosses the phrase 'since we do not establish them' by clarifying that the exclusion of states is not because they are like non-existents, but because the Ashʿarīs simply do not affirm their reality. Finally, the commentator addresses the phrase 'and likewise it necessarily follows, etc.', noting that the author's earlier mention of 'non-existence and existence' was based on a different proof, and that the commentator's own explanation here shows that such pairs are excluded from the definition without redundancy. The commentator also observes that the phrasing 'it necessarily follows that it is excluded' (rather than 'it is excluded') hints that the exclusion is not explicit but logically derived, and that claiming the Necessary (God) is neither identical to nor other than non-existents is absurd.

Key Terms
الغيران
الأحوال
لا نثبتها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: States are excluded because they are non-existent.
Correction: The commentator explicitly says the exclusion is based on not affirming them (lā nuthbituhā), not on the grounds that they are like non-existents.

Checkpoint
Why are states (ahwāl) excluded from the definition of al-ghayrān according to the commentator?
A) Because they are non-existent.
B) Because the Ashʿarīs do not establish them (lā nuthbituhā) and thus they cannot be described as other.
C) Because they are inseparable from their subjects.
D) Because they are identical to their subjects.

Key Takeaway
States are excluded from the definition of 'two different things' because the Ashʿarīs do not affirm their reality, not because they are nonexistent.

Exclusion of Inseparable Pairs: Attribute and Qualified, Part and Whole
Commentator defines the condition of jawāz al-infikāk and gives examples of inseparable pairs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why inseparable pairs like attribute-qualified and part-whole are not considered 'two different things' (ghayrān) in kalam.

Core Idea
Inseparable pairs are neither identical nor truly other.

The definition of 'two different things' (al-ghayrān) includes a key condition: the possibility of separation (jawāz al-infikāk) from both sides. This condition excludes pairs that cannot exist apart, such as an attribute and its qualified subject, or a part and its whole. In this lesson, we explore why such pairs are considered neither identical nor other, and why the permissibility of separation is essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on inseparable pairs
Read the Arabic sentence that introduces the condition of jawāz al-infikāk and the examples of attribute-qualified and part-whole. Then read the translation.
Note the phrase 'lā huwa wa lā ghayruhu' (neither the same nor other).
2
Understand the condition
Understand why the permissibility of separation from both sides is necessary for two things to be considered 'other'. The passage explains that attribute and qualified are not other because they cannot separate.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this matters: if an attribute were considered 'other' than its subject, it would imply it could exist independently, which is not the case.
This connects to the Ashʿarī doctrine of attributes.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An attribute is 'other' than its subject because it is conceptually distinct.
Correction: Conceptual distinctness is not enough; the possibility of existential separation is required. An attribute cannot exist separately from its subject, so it is not 'other'.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is an attribute (al-ṣifa) not considered 'other' than its qualified subject (al-mawṣūf)?
A) Because they are identical.
B) Because separation between them from both sides is not permissible.
C) Because the attribute is non-existent.
D) Because the qualified subject is not a real entity.

Key Takeaway
Inseparable pairs like attribute-qualified are neither identical nor other; the possibility of separation from both sides is essential for otherness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say 'Allāh is Knowing, Allāh is Powerful'—do you ever catch yourself treating His attributes as if they were separate entities added to His essence? After this lesson, how will you actively guard against that mental habit in your worship and understanding of tawḥīd? Write down one concrete way you will remind yourself that His attributes are neither identical to nor other than Him.
?
Consider your own soul and your actions: are your actions 'other' than you? According to the principle of inseparable pairs, what does that imply about your personal responsibility for what you do? How will you change your view of your deeds today based on this lesson?
?
This lesson teaches that existential inseparability negates otherness. Apply this to your relationship with Allāh: you are inseparable from His care at every moment. Does your heart feel that intimacy? If not, what barrier are you placing between yourself and the One upon whom you cannot exist without? Commit to one act of remembrance that acknowledges this inseparability.

5 min
Exclusion of Existent-Non-existent Pairs and the Scope of the Definition
Commentator explains exclusion of existent-non-existent pairs and addition to definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a pair consisting of one existent and one non-existent is excluded from the definition of al-ghayrān, and how the phrase 'in existence or non-existence' broadens the definition to include non-spatially extended things.

Core Idea
Non-existents cannot be 'other' in the full sense, and the definition covers both spatially and non-spatially extended things.

The commentator continues listing exclusions from the definition. First, a pair where one is existent and the other non-existent is necessarily excluded. Then, he discusses an addition to the definition: some scholars include the phrase 'in existence or non-existence' to ensure that non-spatially extended entities like God are covered. This lesson clarifies these two points and the commentator's remarks on the author's phrasing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on existent-non-existent pair
Read the sentence stating that a pair of existent and non-existent is excluded by the definition. Then read the translation.
Note the phrase 'yalzam an yakhruja' indicates necessity.
2
Read the addition about existence or non-existence
Read the part that adds 'in existence or non-existence' to include al-mutaḥayyiz and other things.
This expansion shows the definition aims for comprehensive coverage.
3
Examine the commentator's note on the author's wording
Read the explanation of why the author said 'it necessarily follows that it is excluded' rather than 'it is excluded'. The commentator highlights that the exclusion is not explicit but derived, and that it would be absurd to think otherwise.

المرصد المرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران خرج به الأحوال أيضاً؛ إذ لا نثبتها، فلا يتصور اتصافها بالغيرية. وكذا يلزم أن يخرج به اثنان أحدهما موجود والآخر معدوم . ( و ) خرج بقيد جواز الانفكاك ( ما لا ينفك ) أي ما لا يجوز انفكاكهما ، ( كالصفة مع الموصوف ، والجزء مع الكل، فإنه ) أي المذكور الذي هو الصفة والجزء ( لا هو ولا غيره ) أي ليس الصفة عين الموصوف ولا الجزء عين الكل، وهو ظاهر وليسا أيضاً غير الموصوف، وغير الكل؛ إذ لا يجوز الانفكاك بينهما من الجانبين، وهو معتبر عندهم في الغيرين. (و) قولهم ( في حيز أو عدم ليشمل المتحيز (وغيره وكان الشيخ الأشعري قد عرف معنى قوله : ( إذ لا نثبتها ) أي إخراجهم الأحوال بناء على عدم القول بها، لا بناء على أنها ليست من أفراد الغيرين كالعدمين. وأما ما قيل من أن إخراج ما ليس عندهم مما لا له، فمدفوع بأن المراد خرج ما يقول به البعض. قوله : ( وكذا يلزم إلخ ما مر من قوله : ولا عدم ووجود كان بياناً لعدم كونهما من أفراد المحدود؛ بناء على دليل الشارح قدس سره، دون دليل المصنف وهذا بيان لخروجهما عن الحد، فلا تكرار وإنما قال يلزم أن يخرج، ولم يقل : يخرج إشارة إلى عدم تصريحهم بخروجهما، لكنه يلزم من حدهم وإلى استبعاده، فإن القول بأن الواجب تعالى ليس عين المعدومات ولا غيرها مما يأباه العقل السليم.
The Fourth Observatory - the Seventh Purpose: The two are the different ones. By this [definition] states (al-ahwāl) are also excluded, since we do not establish them, so it is not conceivable that they are described by otherness (al-ghayriyya). Likewise, it necessarily follows that two things, one of which is existent and the other non-existent, are excluded by it. And by the condition of the possibility of separation (jawāz al-infikāk) is excluded what does not separate, i.e., what does not permit their separation, like the attribute (al-ṣifa) with the qualified (al-mawṣūf), and the part (al-juzʾ) with the whole (al-kull). For the mentioned thing, which is the attribute and the part, is neither the same nor other: i.e., the attribute is not identical to the qualified, nor the part identical to the whole, which is obvious, and they are also not other than the qualified and other than the whole, since separation between them from both sides is not permissible, and that [i.e., permissibility of separation from both sides] is considered [valid] for the two different things (al-ghayrān). And their statement 'in existence or non-existence' is to include the spatially extended (al-mutaḥayyiz) and other than it. And Shaykh al-Ashʿarī had defined. His statement: 'since we do not establish them' means their exclusion of states is based on not affirming them, not on the grounds that they are not individuals of the two different things like the two non-existents. As for what was said, that excluding what they do not have is [a case of] what is not for him, it is repelled by [saying] that what is intended is that what some affirm is excluded. His statement: 'and likewise it necessarily follows, etc.' [refers to] what previously passed from his statement 'and not non-existence and existence' as an explanation that they are not individuals of the defined, based on the proof of the commentator (quddisa sirruhu), not on the proof of the author. And this is an explanation of their exclusion from the definition, so there is no repetition. He only said 'it necessarily follows that it is excluded' and did not say 'it is excluded' as an indication that their exclusion is not explicitly stated by them, but it follows necessarily from their definition, and as an indication of its improbability, for the statement that the Necessary (al-wājib taʿālā) is not identical to the non-existents nor other than them is something that sound reason rejects.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of 'al-ghayrān' (two different things). It begins by noting that the definition excludes states (al-ahwāl), because the Ashʿarīs do not affirm states as real entities—they are not established, so they cannot be described as 'other' or 'not other'. Next, it explains that the definition also excludes a pair where one is existent and the other non-existent, since non-existents are not considered individuals of the defined. The main point is that the definition includes a condition: the possibility of separation (jawāz al-infikāk) from both sides. This excludes pairs that cannot be separated, such as an attribute and its qualified subject (e.g., knowledge cannot be separated from the knower), and a part and its whole (e.g., a hand cannot be separated from the body in the sense of being a different entity). Such pairs are neither identical (they are not the same) nor other (they cannot exist apart). The commentator then explains the phrase 'in existence or non-existence' as an addition by some to include spatially extended things and non-spatially extended things under the definition. After quoting Shaykh al-Ashʿarī's definition, the commentator glosses the phrase 'since we do not establish them' by clarifying that the exclusion of states is not because they are like non-existents, but because the Ashʿarīs simply do not affirm their reality. Finally, the commentator addresses the phrase 'and likewise it necessarily follows, etc.', noting that the author's earlier mention of 'non-existence and existence' was based on a different proof, and that the commentator's own explanation here shows that such pairs are excluded from the definition without redundancy. The commentator also observes that the phrasing 'it necessarily follows that it is excluded' (rather than 'it is excluded') hints that the exclusion is not explicit but logically derived, and that claiming the Necessary (God) is neither identical to nor other than non-existents is absurd.

الوجود
العدم
المتحيز
في حيز أو عدم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The definition of al-ghayrān explicitly excludes existent-non-existent pairs in a straightforward statement.
Correction: The commentator notes that the exclusion is not explicit but necessarily follows (yalzam), meaning it is a logical consequence of the definition.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does the author say 'it necessarily follows that it is excluded' (yalzam an yakhruja) instead of 'it is excluded'?
A) To show that the exclusion is explicit in the definition.
B) To indicate that the exclusion is not explicitly stated but logically derived, and to hint at its improbability.
C) To emphasize that the exclusion is only hypothetical.
D) To confuse readers.

Key Takeaway
Pairs of existent and non-existent are necessarily excluded from the definition of al-ghayrān, and the addition 'in existence or non-existence' ensures that the definition applies to all real entities, both spatially extended and not.

The commentator says it is absurd to claim that God is neither identical to non-existents nor other than them. What would it mean to truly affirm that He is real and distinct in a way that no creature can be?

This lesson excludes pairs of existent and non-existent from the definition of 'other'. Objection from Eternal Bodies and the Ashʿarī Revision
Objection from eternal bodies leading to revision of the definition of al-ghayrān.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection from eternal bodies forced a revision to the definition of 'two different things' in kalam, and how the Ashʿarīs used linguistic arguments to support their revised definition.

Core Idea
Eternal bodies cannot cease, so 'difference' must allow for separation in non-existence.

When defining what it means for two things to be 'different' (al-ghayrān), a key condition is that one could cease to exist while the other remains. But what if both are eternal? The objection from eternal bodies challenges this definition, leading the Ashʿarīs to adopt a more precise formulation. In this lesson, we trace the objection, the revision, and a subsequent argument about part and whole.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the passage first to see the objection: two eternal bodies are distinct but cannot cease, contradicting the original definition.
2
Identify the revision
Notice how the definition is changed to what is in the book, the Ashʿarī chosen view. Why does this solve the problem?
3
Examine the part-whole argument
The Ashʿarīs bring a linguistic and legal example to show part and whole are not 'others'. Consider the example of owing ten dirhams.
4
Understand the rebuttal
The argument is countered: the legal judgment may not apply as claimed, and 'other' can refer to a different number.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران مع وجود الآخر، فاعترض عليه بأنا إذا فرضنا جسمين قديمين كانا متغايرين بالضرورة مع أنه لا يجوز عدم أحدهما مع وجود الآخر. فإن العدم ينافي القدم، فغير التعريف إلى ما في الكتاب، وهو المختار عند الأشاعرة . قالوا : دل الشرع واللغة على أن الجزء والكل ليسا غيرين، فإنك إذا قلت : ليس له علي غير عشرة يحكم عليك بلزوم الخمسة، فلو كان الجزء غير الكل لما كان كذلك. ورد عليه بأن المراد أما الخمسة فقط فلا نسلم الحكم بلزومها، وأما مع تمام آحاد العشرة، فذلك هو العشرة نفسها، وبأن الغير هاهنا محمول على عدد آخر
The Fourth Observatory - the Seventh Purpose: The two are the different ones with the existence of the other. Then it was objected against it: that if we suppose two bodies that are eternal (qadīmayn), they are necessarily different (mutaghāyirān) while it is not permissible for one of them to cease to exist with the existence of the other. For non-existence (al-ʿadam) is incompatible with eternality (al-qidam). So he changed the definition to what is in the book, and it is the chosen [view] of the Ashʿarīs. They said: religious law (al-sharʿ) and language (al-lugha) indicate that the part and the whole are not two different things. For if you say 'He does not have any other than ten dirhams against me,' the judgment is that you are liable for five. If the part were other than the whole, it would not be so. And it was responded against it that what is meant: as for the five alone, we do not concede the judgment of liability; and as for with the completion of the individuals of ten, that is the ten itself; and because 'other' (al-ghayr) here is predicated of another number.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the definition of al-ghayrān (two different things) and the Ashʿarī response that leads to a revision. The objection is: if we consider two bodies that are eternal (qadīmayn), they are necessarily distinct from each other (mutaghāyirān), yet it is impossible for one to cease to exist while the other exists, because non-existence (ʿadam) is incompatible with eternality (qidam). Since the original definition required that it be possible for one to cease while the other exists, eternal bodies would violate the definition even though they are clearly distinct. Therefore, the definition must be changed. The Ashʿarīs adopted a revised definition that includes the possibility of separation in non-existence as well (i.e., it is possible for one to be non-existent while the other exists, or for one to exist while the other is non-existent). The passage then brings a linguistic and legal argument: the part (juzʾ) and the whole (kull) are not considered 'others'. For example, if someone says 'I owe him no other than ten dirhams,' the obligation is for five dirhams (since ten includes five). If the part were 'other' than the whole, then saying 'no other than ten' would not entail liability for five. This argument is then rebutted: if by 'five' you mean the five alone (without the rest), the legal judgment is not conceded; if you mean the five along with the other five, that is exactly the ten itself. Moreover, 'other' in this phrase refers to a different number (i.e., ten is not a different entity from five but includes it). The commentator's explanation clarifies that the objection forced a modification to the definition, and the Ashʿarīs adopted the revised form that appears in the book (al-Mawaqif).

Key Terms
جسمان قديمان
العدم ينافي القدم
التعريف
المختار عند الأشاعرة
الجزء والكل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The definition of 'other' only requires possible separation in existence.
Correction: The objection shows that for eternal entities, separation in non-existence is also needed, leading to the revised Ashʿarī definition.

Checkpoint
What was the objection against the original definition of al-ghayrān that led the Ashʿarīs to revise it?
A) It did not account for part-whole relationships.
B) It failed to include non-existents as individuals.
C) Two eternal bodies are distinct but cannot cease to exist, contradicting the condition of possible cessation.
D) The definition was based on language rather than logic.

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'two different things' must account for both existential and non-existential separation; the Ashʿarīs revised it to accommodate eternal entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The definition of 'different' was revised when it failed to account for eternal beings. In your understanding of tawḥīd, have you ever held a definition of Allah that was too narrow or based only on your own experience? How might you revise it to better reflect His absolute uniqueness?
?
The Ashʿarīs used language evidence to show that part and whole are not 'others'. Consider your own life: are there areas you try to separate from your identity (e.g., your sins, your weaknesses) as if they are 'other' than you? How does the Qur'an's teaching that everything returns to Allah challenge you to accept full responsibility before Him?

Definition of Two Different Things and Response to Objection
Defines 'two different things' and responds to objection about relational concepts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of 'two different things' (الغَيْرَان) in Islamic theology and how the objection regarding relational concepts is resolved.

Core Idea
Difference requires possible separation; relations are mental, not real existents.

In this passage, the author establishes a precise definition of what it means for two things to be 'different' or 'other' (غَيْر). This definition has important implications for understanding God's attributes. The author then addresses a potential objection involving relational concepts like fatherhood and sonship, which seem to be different yet inseparable.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
The author begins by defining 'two different things' (الاثنان هما الغيران). Note the key condition: it is possible (يجوز) for them to be separated in some respect (بوجه).
The phrase 'عين ولا غير' might be corrupt; focus on the main definition.
2
Apply the definition to divine attributes
See how this definition applies to the essential attributes of God (الصفات النفسية). Since they cannot be separated from each other, they are neither identical nor entirely other.
3
Understand the objection
An objection is raised: relational concepts like fatherhood and sonship are different but cannot be separated in non-existence or location. Identify the objection's logic.
4
See the response
The author responds that these relations are non-existent (غير موجودين); they are merely mental considerations (أمور اعتبارية). Since the definition requires both things to be existent, the objection does not apply.
This shows the importance of ontology in theological definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران. عين ولا غير. وهي ما انفكاكه عنه بوجه كالعلم والقدرة والإرادة وغير ذلك يمتنع من الصفات النفسية لله تعالى بناء على أن معنى المتغايرين موجودان يجوز الانفكاك بينهما بوجه وعلى هذا فتلك الصفات النفسانية لما امتنع انفكاك بعضها عن بعض لم يقل إن بعضها عين الصفة الأخرى، أو غيرها. وأورد عليهم المضافان كالأبوة والبنوة، والعلية والمعلولية فإنهما متغايران مع امتناع الانفكاك من الجانبين في العدم؛ إذ لا يجوز أن يعدم أحدهما ويوجد الآخر، وفي الحيز أيضاً، إذ ليسا بمتحيزين. ولا يلزمهم فإنهما غير موجودين؛ لأن النسب والإضافات أمور اعتبارية لا وجود لها عندهم.
The Fourth Observation - Seventh Section: The two are the two different things. 'Ayn and not ghayr. And it is that whose separation from it is possible in some respect, like knowledge, power, will, and other than that which is impossible from the essential attributes of Allah Almighty, based on the meaning of two different things being two existents such that separation between them is possible in some respect. And on this basis, those essential attributes, since separation of some from others is impossible, it is not said that some of them are identical to the other attribute or other than it. And they object with the two relatives, like fatherhood and sonship, and causality and effect, for they are two different things despite the impossibility of separation from both sides in non-existence; for it is not possible that one of them cease to exist and the other exist, and also in location, since they are not located. But it does not apply to them because they are non-existent; for relations and additions are mental considerations that have no existence according to them.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'two different things' (الغيران). The definition states that two things are considered different if it is possible for them to be separated from each other in some respect (بوجه). The author then applies this to the essential attributes of God, noting that since these attributes cannot be separated from each other, they are neither identical to nor other than each other. An objection is raised regarding relational concepts (المضافان) like fatherhood and sonship, which seem to be different but cannot be separated from each other in non-existence or location. The response is that such relations are not real existents (موجودان); they are merely mental considerations (أمور اعتبارية), and the definition of 'different things' requires both to be existent. Therefore, the objection does not apply.

Key Terms
الاثنان هما الغيران
الانفكاك
الصفات النفسية
المضافان
أمور اعتبارية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Relational concepts like fatherhood and sonship are existent things that violate the definition of difference.
Correction: Such relations are non-existent; they are mental considerations (أمور اعتبارية) and thus do not meet the requirement that both things be existent.

Checkpoint
What is the condition for two things to be considered 'different' (غَيْرَان) according to the definition given?
A) They must be separable in both existence and location.
B) It must be possible to separate them in some respect.
C) They must always be actually separated.
D) They must be different in essence.

Key Takeaway
Two things are 'different' only if they can be separated in some respect, and this definition holds only for real existents, not mental constructs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How would that shift affect your daily interactions?
?
The essential attributes of God are inseparable. Now consider your own attributes: your knowledge, your will, your desires. Are they truly separable? How often do you act as if they are independent—following desire without knowledge, or knowing without willing? What does this lesson teach you about the integration of your inner qualities, and how will you pursue greater coherence in your character starting today?

If the definition of 'difference' requires possible separation, and God's attributes are perfectly united, then your understanding of God must not fragment Him into separate parts. Definition of Ghayrān and Conceptual Separation from Both Sides
Discusses definition of ghayrān and objection on attributes and parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct definition of two things being 'other' (ghayrān) and why it requires conceptual separation from both sides.

Core Idea
Two things are 'other' only if they can be conceptually separated from both sides.

This lesson examines a key definition in kalam: what does it mean for two things to be 'other'? The author establishes that the criterion is not actual existence but conceptual separation. An objection regarding attributes and parts is raised and answered, reinforcing the need for separation from both sides in thought, not in reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the initial claim about separation from one side and the subsequent objection.
Notice that the passage begins by stating that separation from one side in non-existence or location is sufficient.
2
Identify the objection
Identify the objection: if separation from one side sufficed, then attributes would be 'other' than their subjects, and parts 'other' than wholes—a consequence not accepted in Islamic theology.
3
Understand the answer
Understand that the answer clarifies that the intended separation is conceptual (ta'aqqulan), not existential, thereby preserving the definition without unwanted implications.
Thus, two things can be 'other' in thought even if they cannot exist separately in reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : الاثنان هما الغيران ٠٧ ولا يجوز شيء منهما على الباري، فقد جاز الانفكاك بينهما من أحد الجانبين في كل واحد من العدم والحيز مع أن جواز الانفكاك عنه في العدم فقط، أو الحيز فقط كان كافياً في دخولهما في الحد. لأنا) نقول : لو كفى الانفكاك من طرف) في الاتصاف بالغيرية ( لجاز انفكاك الموصوف عن صفته والجزء عن الكل في الوجود ) أي لكان جواز انفكاك الموصوف عن صفته في الوجود، بأن يوجد الموصوف وتعدم الصفة كافياً في تغايرهما لأنه جاز حينئذ انفكاك أحدهما عن الآخر في العدم. وحيث كان الجواب السابق الذي ذكره الآمدي مردوداً بما ذكرناه (فقيل) في الجواب عن الإيراد : ( المراد جواز الانفكاك ) من الجانبين (تعقلاً) لا وجوداً . (ومنهم من صرح به)، فقال: الانفكاك
The Fourth Observatory - The Seventh Purpose: The two [things] are the two others. 07 And it is not permissible for any of them to be attributed to the Creator, for separation between them from one side in each of non-existence and location is permissible, even though the permissibility of separation from it in non-existence only or location only was sufficient for their inclusion in the definition. For we say: If the separation from one side sufficed for the description of otherness, then the separation of the described from its attribute and the part from the whole in existence would be permissible, meaning that the permissibility of separation of the described from its attribute in existence, such that the described exists and the attribute is non-existent, would suffice for their being other because then the separation of one from the other in non-existence would be permissible. And since the previous answer mentioned by al-Amidi is refuted by what we have mentioned, it was said in response to the objection: 'What is intended is the permissibility of separation from both sides conceptually, not existentially.' And some of them explicitly stated it, saying: 'Separation...'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage addresses the definition of two things being 'other' (ghayrān). It begins by stating that it is not permissible for either of the two things to be attributed to the Creator, meaning that they must be other than Him. The key point is whether separation from one side (in non-existence or location) is sufficient for otherness. The objection is raised that if separation from one side suffices, then attributes would be other than their subjects, and parts other than wholes, which is not accepted in kalam. The answer is that the intended meaning is separation from both sides conceptually (ta'aqqulan), not in actual existence. This resolves the objection, as conceptual separation does not require actual existence. The passage then notes that some scholars explicitly state this position.

الانفكاك
تعقلاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that separation in actual existence is required for two things to be 'other'.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only conceptual separation (ta'aqqulan) from both sides is required, not existential separation.

Checkpoint

B) Separation in non-existence from one side
C) Conceptual separation from both sides
D) Either existential or conceptual separation

Key Takeaway
Two things are considered 'other' only if they can be conceptually separated from both sides, not necessarily in actual existence.

Alternative Definition of Ghayrān and the Need for Proof of God
Defines ghayrān as known independently and discusses the need for proof of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternative definition of ghayrān (two things that are other) as those that can be known independently, and how this definition leads to the conclusion that the existence of God requires proof from the existence of the world.

Core Idea
Two things are other if they can be known separately — explaining why the world alone doesn't prove God without a demonstration.

This passage introduces a refined definition of what it means for two things to be 'other' (ghayrān). Instead of requiring separation in existence, it requires only conceptual independence. This definition becomes critical when we consider the world and its Creator: we can conceive of the world without conceiving of God, and vice versa. That is why, according to the author, we need a formal proof to establish God's existence from the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the key terms: ghayrān, 'ilm (knowledge), jahl (ignorance), ta'aqqul (conception). The definition states that two things are 'other' when each can be known while the other is unknown.
The definition does not require them to be separate in existence.
2
Apply to the world and Creator
The passage applies this definition: one can conceive of the world and be certain of its existence without conceiving of the Creator and being certain of His existence. Therefore, the existence of the Creator after knowing the world requires a proof (burhān). Understand why this follows from the definition.
This is the key point: conceptual independence means God's existence is not self-evident from the world.
3
Clarify conceptual vs. existential separation
The passage clarifies that the separation meant is in conception, not in existence. Although the world cannot exist without the Creator, they can be conceived independently. This answers a potential objection.
Note also the warning: if a condition of non-existence or location were added to the definition, the answer would not hold.

The two others are those for which knowledge of each is permissible with ignorance of the other, and it is not impossible to conceive of the world and be certain of its existence without conceiving of the Creator and being certain of His existence, and therefore the existence of the Creator after knowledge of the existence of the world requires proof by demonstration. Commentary
This passage presents an alternative definition of ghayrān (two things that are other): they are things each of which can be known while being ignorant of the other. This definition avoids the earlier issue of separation from both sides in existence, as it focuses on conceptual independence. The passage then applies this to the relationship between the world and the Creator: one can conceive of the world without conceiving of the Creator, and vice versa. This is why proof is needed to establish the existence of the Creator from the existence of the world. The passage further discusses the condition of separation from both sides in conceptualization, noting that if a condition of non-existence or location were added to the definition, the answer would not hold. It then examines the objection concerning some attributes (e.g., speech and power) that can be conceived independently yet are not considered other, and the objection that this definition would sever the necessary connection between smoke and fire. The commentator defends the definition by noting that the intended conceptual separation does not require conceiving the other as non-existent, and that the definition is a reformulation to avoid earlier objections.
